     651      425770 : inline std::complex<double> airy(
     652             :     std::complex<double> z,
     653             :     int id,
     654             :     int kode,
     655             :     int *nz,
     656             :     int *ierr
     657             : ) {
     658             : 
     659             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZAIRY
     660             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
     661             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
     662             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
     663             :     //***KEYWORDS  AIRY FUNCTION,BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF ORDER ONE THIRD
     664             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
     665             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE AIRY FUNCTIONS AI(Z) AND DAI(Z) FOR COMPLEX Z
     666             :     //***DESCRIPTION
     667             :     //
     668             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
     669             :     //         ON KODE=1, ZAIRY COMPUTES THE COMPLEX AIRY FUNCTION AI(Z) OR
     670             :     //         ITS DERIVATIVE DAI(Z)/DZ ON ID=0 OR ID=1 RESPECTIVELY. ON
     671             :     //         KODE=2, A SCALING OPTION CEXP(ZTA)*AI(Z) OR CEXP(ZTA)*
     672             :     //         DAI(Z)/DZ IS PROVIDED TO REMOVE THE EXPONENTIAL DECAY IN
     673             :     //         -PI/3.LT.ARG(Z).LT.PI/3 AND THE EXPONENTIAL GROWTH IN
     674             :     //         PI/3.LT.ABS(ARG(Z)).LT.PI WHERE ZTA=(2/3)*Z*CSQRT(Z).
     675             :     //
     676             :     //         WHILE THE AIRY FUNCTIONS AI(Z) AND DAI(Z)/DZ ARE ANALYTIC IN
     677             :     //         THE WHOLE Z PLANE, THE CORRESPONDING SCALED FUNCTIONS DEFINED
     678             :     //         FOR KODE=2 HAVE A CUT ALONG THE NEGATIVE REAL AXIS.
     679             :     //         DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF
     680             :     //         MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS (REF. 1).
     681             :     //
     682             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
     683             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI)
     684             :     //           ID     - ORDER OF DERIVATIVE, ID=0 OR ID=1
     685             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
     686             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
     687             :     //                             AI=AI(Z)                ON ID=0 OR
     688             :     //                             AI=DAI(Z)/DZ            ON ID=1
     689             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
     690             :     //                             AI=CEXP(ZTA)*AI(Z)       ON ID=0 OR
     691             :     //                             AI=CEXP(ZTA)*DAI(Z)/DZ   ON ID=1 WHERE
     692             :     //                             ZTA=(2/3)*Z*CSQRT(Z)
     693             :     //
     694             :     //         OUTPUT     AIR,AII ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
     695             :     //           AIR,AII- COMPLEX ANSWER DEPENDING ON THE CHOICES FOR ID AND
     696             :     //                    KODE
     697             :     //           NZ     - UNDERFLOW INDICATOR
     698             :     //                    NZ= 0   , NORMAL RETURN
     699             :     //                    NZ= 1   , AI=std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0) DUE TO UNDERFLOW IN
     700             :     //                              -PI/3.LT.ARG(Z).LT.PI/3 ON KODE=1
     701             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
     702             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
     703             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
     704             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, REAL(ZTA)
     705             :     //                            TOO LARGE ON KODE=1
     706             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) LARGE      - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
     707             :     //                            LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
     708             :     //                            PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE ACCURACY
     709             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) TOO LARGE  - NO COMPUTATION
     710             :     //                            COMPLETE LOSS OF ACCURACY BY ARGUMENT
     711             :     //                            REDUCTION
     712             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
     713             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
     714             :     //
     715             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
     716             :     //
     717             :     //         AI AND DAI ARE COMPUTED FOR CABS(Z).GT.1.0 FROM THE K BESSEL
     718             :     //         FUNCTIONS BY
     719             :     //
     720             :     //            AI(Z)=C*SQRT(Z)*K(1/3,ZTA) , DAI(Z)=-C*Z*K(2/3,ZTA)
     721             :     //                           C=1.0/(PI*SQRT(3.0))
     722             :     //                            ZTA=(2/3)*Z**(3/2)
     723             :     //
     724             :     //         WITH THE POWER SERIES FOR CABS(Z).LE.1.0.
     725             :     //
     726             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
     727             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z IS LARGE, LOSSES
     728             :     //         OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR. CONSEQUENTLY, IF
     729             :     //         THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA=(2/3)*Z**1.5 EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR),
     730             :     //         THEN LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR
     731             :     //         FLAG IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
     732             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
     733             :     //         ALSO, IF THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN
     734             :     //         ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT
     735             :     //         FUNCTION, ZETA MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE
     736             :     //         LARGEST INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA
     737             :     //         MUST BE RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2,
     738             :     //         AND U3 ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE
     739             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE
     740             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMIT-
     741             :     //         ING IN THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT THE MAG-
     742             :     //         NITUDE OF Z CANNOT EXCEED 3.1E+4 IN SINGLE AND 2.1E+6 IN
     743             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC. THIS ALSO MEANS THAT ONE CAN
     744             :     //         EXPECT TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES,
     745             :     //         NO DIGITS IN SINGLE PRECISION AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE
     746             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC. SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER
     747             :     //         MACHINES.
     748             :     //
     749             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
     750             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
     751             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
     752             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
     753             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
     754             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
     755             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
     756             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
     757             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
     758             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
     759             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
     760             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
     761             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
     762             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
     763             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
     764             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
     765             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,

    1126             : 
    1127       14369 : inline int besh(
    1128             :     std::complex<double> z,
    1129             :     double fnu,
    1130             :     int kode,
    1131             :     int m,
    1132             :     int n,
    1133             :     std::complex<double> *cy,
    1134             :     int *ierr
    1135             : ) {
    1136             : 
    1137             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBESH
    1138             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    1139             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    1140             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    1141             :     //***KEYWORDS  H-BESSEL FUNCTIONS,BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT,
    1142             :     //             BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF THIRD KIND,HANKEL FUNCTIONS
    1143             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    1144             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE THE H-BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1145             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    1146             :     //
    1147             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    1148             :     //         ON KODE=1, ZBESH COMPUTES AN N MEMBER SEQUENCE OF COMPLEX
    1149             :     //         HANKEL (BESSEL) FUNCTIONS CY(J)=H(M,FNU+J-1,Z) FOR KINDS M=1
    1150             :     //         OR 2, REAL, NONNEGATIVE ORDERS FNU+J-1, J=1,...,N, AND COMPLEX
    1151             :     //         Z.NE.std::complex<double>(0.0,0.0) IN THE CUT PLANE -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI.
    1152             :     //         ON KODE=2, ZBESH RETURNS THE SCALED HANKEL FUNCTIONS
    1153             :     //
    1154             :     //         CY(I)=EXP(-MM*Z*I)*H(M,FNU+J-1,Z)       MM=3-2*M,   I**2=-1.
    1155             :     //
    1156             :     //         WHICH REMOVES THE EXPONENTIAL BEHAVIOR IN BOTH THE UPPER AND
    1157             :     //         LOWER HALF PLANES. DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION ARE FOUND IN THE
    1158             :     //         NBS HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS (REF. 1).
    1159             :     //
    1160             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI,FNU ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1161             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI), Z.NE.std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0),
    1162             :     //                    -PT.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI
    1163             :     //           FNU    - ORDER OF INITIAL H FUNCTION, FNU.GE.0.0D0
    1164             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    1165             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    1166             :     //                             CY(J)=H(M,FNU+J-1,Z),   J=1,...,N
    1167             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    1168             :     //                             CY(J)=H(M,FNU+J-1,Z)*EXP(-I*Z*(3-2M))
    1169             :     //                                  J=1,...,N  ,  I**2=-1
    1170             :     //           M      - KIND OF HANKEL FUNCTION, M=1 OR 2
    1171             :     //           N      - NUMBER OF MEMBERS IN THE SEQUENCE, N.GE.1
    1172             :     //
    1173             :     //         OUTPUT     CYR,CYI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1174             :     //           CYR,CYI- DOUBLE PRECISION VECTORS WHOSE FIRST N COMPONENTS
    1175             :     //                    CONTAIN REAL AND IMAGINARY PARTS FOR THE SEQUENCE
    1176             :     //                    CY(J)=H(M,FNU+J-1,Z)  OR
    1177             :     //                    CY(J)=H(M,FNU+J-1,Z)*EXP(-I*Z*(3-2M))  J=1,...,N
    1178             :     //                    DEPENDING ON KODE, I**2=-1.
    1179             :     //           NZ     - NUMBER OF COMPONENTS SET TO ZERO DUE TO UNDERFLOW,
    1180             :     //                    NZ= 0   , NORMAL RETURN
    1181             :     //                    NZ.GT.0 , FIRST NZ COMPONENTS OF CY SET TO ZERO DUE
    1182             :     //                              TO UNDERFLOW, CY(J)=std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0)
    1183             :     //                              J=1,...,NZ WHEN Y.GT.0.0 AND M=1 OR
    1184             :     //                              Y.LT.0.0 AND M=2. FOR THE COMPLMENTARY
    1185             :     //                              HALF PLANES, NZ STATES ONLY THE NUMBER
    1186             :     //                              OF UNDERFLOWS.
    1187             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    1188             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    1189             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    1190             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, FNU TOO
    1191             :     //                            LARGE OR CABS(Z) TOO SMALL OR BOTH
    1192             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 LARGE - COMPUTATION DONE
    1193             :     //                            BUT LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT
    1194             :     //                            REDUCTION PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE
    1195             :     //                            ACCURACY
    1196             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 TOO LARGE - NO COMPUTA-
    1197             :     //                            TION BECAUSE OF COMPLETE LOSSES OF SIGNIFI-
    1198             :     //                            CANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    1199             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    1200             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    1201             :     //
    1202             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    1203             :     //
    1204             :     //         THE COMPUTATION IS CARRIED OUT BY THE RELATION
    1205             :     //
    1206             :     //         H(M,FNU,Z)=(1/MP)*EXP(-MP*FNU)*K(FNU,Z*EXP(-MP))
    1207             :     //             MP=MM*HPI*I,  MM=3-2*M,  HPI=PI/2,  I**2=-1
    1208             :     //
    1209             :     //         FOR M=1 OR 2 WHERE THE K BESSEL FUNCTION IS COMPUTED FOR THE
    1210             :     //         RIGHT HALF PLANE RE(Z).GE.0.0. THE K FUNCTION IS CONTINUED
    1211             :     //         TO THE LEFT HALF PLANE BY THE RELATION
    1212             :     //
    1213             :     //         K(FNU,Z*EXP(MP)) = EXP(-MP*FNU)*K(FNU,Z)-MP*I(FNU,Z)
    1214             :     //         MP=MR*PI*I, MR=+1 OR -1, RE(Z).GT.0, I**2=-1
    1215             :     //
    1216             :     //         WHERE I(FNU,Z) IS THE I BESSEL FUNCTION.
    1217             :     //
    1218             :     //         EXPONENTIAL DECAY OF H(M,FNU,Z) OCCURS IN THE UPPER HALF Z
    1219             :     //         PLANE FOR M=1 AND THE LOWER HALF Z PLANE FOR M=2.  EXPONENTIAL
    1220             :     //         GROWTH OCCURS IN THE COMPLEMENTARY HALF PLANES.  SCALING
    1221             :     //         BY EXP(-MM*Z*I) REMOVES THE EXPONENTIAL BEHAVIOR IN THE
    1222             :     //         WHOLE Z PLANE FOR Z TO INFINITY.
    1223             :     //
    1224             :     //         FOR NEGATIVE ORDERS,THE FORMULAE
    1225             :     //
    1226             :     //               H(1,-FNU,Z) = H(1,FNU,Z)*CEXP( PI*FNU*I)
    1227             :     //               H(2,-FNU,Z) = H(2,FNU,Z)*CEXP(-PI*FNU*I)
    1228             :     //                         I**2=-1
    1229             :     //
    1230             :     //         CAN BE USED.
    1231             :     //
    1232             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    1233             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z OR FNU+N-1 IS
    1234             :     //         LARGE, LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR.
    1235             :     //         CONSEQUENTLY, IF EITHER ONE EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR), THEN
    1236             :     //         LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR FLAG
    1237             :     //         IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    1238             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    1239             :     //         IF EITHER IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS
    1240             :     //         LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT FUNCTION, ARGUMENTS
    1241             :     //         MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE LARGEST MACHINE
    1242             :     //         INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF Z AND FNU+N-1 IS
    1243             :     //         RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2, AND U3
    1244             :     //         ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE PRECISION
    1245             :     //         ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE PRECISION
    1246             :     //         ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMITING IN
    1247             :     //         THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT ONE CAN EXPECT
    1248             :     //         TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES, NO DIGITS
    1249             :     //         IN SINGLE AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC.
    1250             :     //         SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER MACHINES.
    1251             :     //
    1252             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    1253             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    1254             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0D-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    1255             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    1256             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    1257             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    1258             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    1259             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    1260             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    1261             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    1262             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    1263             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    1264             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    1265             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    1266             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    1267             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    1268             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    1269             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,
    1270             :     //         OR -PI/2+P.
    1271             :     //
    1272             :     //***REFERENCES  HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS BY M. ABRAMOWITZ
    1273             :     //                 AND I. A. STEGUN, NBS AMS SERIES 55, U.S. DEPT. OF
    1274             :     //                 COMMERCE, 1955.
    1275             :     //
    1276             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1277             :     //                 BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0083, MAY, 1983.
    1278             :     //
    1279             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1280             :     //                 AND LARGE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0643, MAY, 1983
    1281             :     //
    1282             :     //               A SUBROUTINE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    1283             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND85-
    1284             :     //                 1018, MAY, 1985
    1285             :     //
    1286             :     //               A PORTABLE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    1287             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, TRANS.
    1288             :     //                 MATH. SOFTWARE, 1986
    1289             :     //
    1290             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  ZACON,ZBKNU,ZBUNK,ZUOIK,AZABS,I1MACH,D1MACH
    1291             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZBESH
    1292             :

    1296             :         bb, ascle, rtol, atol;

    1470             : 
    1471        7453 : inline int besi(
    1472             :     std::complex<double> z,
    1473             :     double fnu,
    1474             :     int kode,
    1475             :     int n,
    1476             :     std::complex<double> *cy,
    1477             :     int *ierr
    1478             : ) {
    1479             : 
    1480             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBESI
    1481             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    1482             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    1483             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    1484             :     //***KEYWORDS  I-BESSEL FUNCTION,COMPLEX BESSEL FUNCTION,
    1485             :     //             MODIFIED BESSEL FUNCTION OF THE FIRST KIND
    1486             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    1487             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE I-BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1488             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    1489             :     //
    1490             :     //                    ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    1491             :     //         ON KODE=1, ZBESI COMPUTES AN N MEMBER SEQUENCE OF COMPLEX
    1492             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTIONS CY(J)=I(FNU+J-1,Z) FOR REAL, NONNEGATIVE
    1493             :     //         ORDERS FNU+J-1, J=1,...,N AND COMPLEX Z IN THE CUT PLANE
    1494             :     //         -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI. ON KODE=2, ZBESI RETURNS THE SCALED
    1495             :     //         FUNCTIONS
    1496             :     //
    1497             :     //         CY(J)=EXP(-ABS(X))*I(FNU+J-1,Z)   J = 1,...,N , X=REAL(Z)
    1498             :     //
    1499             :     //         WITH THE EXPONENTIAL GROWTH REMOVED IN BOTH THE LEFT AND
    1500             :     //         RIGHT HALF PLANES FOR Z TO INFINITY. DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION
    1501             :     //         ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS
    1502             :     //         (REF. 1).
    1503             :     //
    1504             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI,FNU ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1505             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI),  -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI
    1506             :     //           FNU    - ORDER OF INITIAL I FUNCTION, FNU.GE.0.0D0
    1507             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    1508             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    1509             :     //                             CY(J)=I(FNU+J-1,Z), J=1,...,N
    1510             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    1511             :     //                             CY(J)=I(FNU+J-1,Z)*EXP(-ABS(X)), J=1,...,N
    1512             :     //           N      - NUMBER OF MEMBERS OF THE SEQUENCE, N.GE.1
    1513             :     //
    1514             :     //         OUTPUT     CYR,CYI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1515             :     //           CYR,CYI- DOUBLE PRECISION VECTORS WHOSE FIRST N COMPONENTS
    1516             :     //                    CONTAIN REAL AND IMAGINARY PARTS FOR THE SEQUENCE
    1517             :     //                    CY(J)=I(FNU+J-1,Z)  OR
    1518             :     //                    CY(J)=I(FNU+J-1,Z)*EXP(-ABS(X))  J=1,...,N
    1519             :     //                    DEPENDING ON KODE, X=REAL(Z)
    1520             :     //           NZ     - NUMBER OF COMPONENTS SET TO ZERO DUE TO UNDERFLOW,
    1521             :     //                    NZ= 0   , NORMAL RETURN
    1522             :     //                    NZ.GT.0 , LAST NZ COMPONENTS OF CY SET TO ZERO
    1523             :     //                              TO UNDERFLOW, CY(J)=std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0)
    1524             :     //                              J = N-NZ+1,...,N
    1525             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    1526             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    1527             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    1528             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, REAL(Z) TOO
    1529             :     //                            LARGE ON KODE=1
    1530             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 LARGE - COMPUTATION DONE
    1531             :     //                            BUT LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT
    1532             :     //                            REDUCTION PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE
    1533             :     //                            ACCURACY
    1534             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 TOO LARGE - NO COMPUTA-
    1535             :     //                            TION BECAUSE OF COMPLETE LOSSES OF SIGNIFI-
    1536             :     //                            CANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    1537             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    1538             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    1539             :     //
    1540             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    1541             :     //
    1542             :     //         THE COMPUTATION IS CARRIED OUT BY THE POWER SERIES FOR
    1543             :     //         SMALL CABS(Z), THE ASYMPTOTIC EXPANSION FOR LARGE CABS(Z),
    1544             :     //         THE MILLER ALGORITHM NORMALIZED BY THE WRONSKIAN AND A
    1545             :     //         NEUMANN SERIES FOR IMTERMEDIATE MAGNITUDES, AND THE
    1546             :     //         UNIFORM ASYMPTOTIC EXPANSIONS FOR I(FNU,Z) AND J(FNU,Z)
    1547             :     //         FOR LARGE ORDERS. BACKWARD RECURRENCE IS USED TO GENERATE
    1548             :     //         SEQUENCES OR REDUCE ORDERS WHEN NECESSARY.
    1549             :     //
    1550             :     //         THE CALCULATIONS ABOVE ARE DONE IN THE RIGHT HALF PLANE AND
    1551             :     //         CONTINUED INTO THE LEFT HALF PLANE BY THE FORMULA
    1552             :     //
    1553             :     //         I(FNU,Z*EXP(M*PI)) = EXP(M*PI*FNU)*I(FNU,Z)  REAL(Z).GT.0.0
    1554             :     //                       M = +I OR -I,  I**2=-1
    1555             :     //
    1556             :     //         FOR NEGATIVE ORDERS,THE FORMULA
    1557             :     //
    1558             :     //              I(-FNU,Z) = I(FNU,Z) + (2/PI)*SIN(PI*FNU)*K(FNU,Z)
    1559             :     //
    1560             :     //         CAN BE USED. HOWEVER,FOR LARGE ORDERS CLOSE TO INTEGERS, THE
    1561             :     //         THE FUNCTION CHANGES RADICALLY. WHEN FNU IS A LARGE POSITIVE
    1562             :     //         INTEGER,THE MAGNITUDE OF I(-FNU,Z)=I(FNU,Z) IS A LARGE
    1563             :     //         NEGATIVE POWER OF TEN. BUT WHEN FNU IS NOT AN INTEGER,
    1564             :     //         K(FNU,Z) DOMINATES IN MAGNITUDE WITH A LARGE POSITIVE POWER OF
    1565             :     //         TEN AND THE MOST THAT THE SECOND TERM CAN BE REDUCED IS BY
    1566             :     //         UNIT ROUNDOFF FROM THE COEFFICIENT. THUS, WIDE CHANGES CAN
    1567             :     //         OCCUR WITHIN UNIT ROUNDOFF OF A LARGE INTEGER FOR FNU. HERE,
    1568             :     //         LARGE MEANS FNU.GT.CABS(Z).
    1569             :     //
    1570             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    1571             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z OR FNU+N-1 IS
    1572             :     //         LARGE, LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR.
    1573             :     //         CONSEQUENTLY, IF EITHER ONE EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR), THEN
    1574             :     //         LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR FLAG
    1575             :     //         IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    1576             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    1577             :     //         IF EITHER IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS
    1578             :     //         LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT FUNCTION, ARGUMENTS
    1579             :     //         MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE LARGEST MACHINE
    1580             :     //         INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF Z AND FNU+N-1 IS
    1581             :     //         RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2, AND U3
    1582             :     //         ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE PRECISION
    1583             :     //         ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE PRECISION
    1584             :     //         ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMITING IN
    1585             :     //         THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT ONE CAN EXPECT
    1586             :     //         TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES, NO DIGITS
    1587             :     //         IN SINGLE AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC.
    1588             :     //         SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER MACHINES.
    1589             :     //
    1590             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    1591             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    1592             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    1593             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    1594             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    1595             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    1596             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    1597             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    1598             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    1599             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    1600             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    1601             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    1602             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    1603             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    1604             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    1605             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    1606             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    1607             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,
    1608             :     //         OR -PI/2+P.
    1609             :     //
    1610             :     //***REFERENCES  HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS BY M. ABRAMOWITZ
    1611             :     //                 AND I. A. STEGUN, NBS AMS SERIES 55, U.S. DEPT. OF
    1612             :     //                 COMMERCE, 1955.
    1613             :     //
    1614             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1615             :     //                 BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0083, MAY, 1983.
    1616             :     //
    1617             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1618             :     //                 AND LARGE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0643, MAY, 1983
    1619             :     //
    1620             :     //               A SUBROUTINE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    1621             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND85-
    1622             :     //                 1018, MAY, 1985
    1623             :     //
    1624             :     //               A PORTABLE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    1625             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, TRANS.
    1626             :     //                 MATH. SOFTWARE, 1986
    1627             :     //
    1628             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  ZBINU,I1MACH,D1MACH
    1629             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZBESI
    1630             : 
    1631        7453 :     std::complex<double> csgn, zn;
    1632        7453 :     double aa, alim, arg, atol, ascle, az, bb, dig, elim, fn, fnul, rl, rtol,\
    1633             :            r1m5, tol, xx, yy;
    1634        7453 :     int i, inu, k, k1, k2, nn, nz;
    1635        7453 :     double pi = 3.14159265358979324;
    1636             : 
    1637        7453 :     *ierr = 0;
    1638        7453 :     nz = 0;
    1639        7453 :     if (fnu < 0.0) { *ierr = 1; }
    1640        7453 :     if ((kode < 1) || (kode > 2)) { *ierr = 1; }
    1641        7453 :     if (n < 1) { *ierr = 1; }
    1642        7453 :     if (*ierr != 0) { return nz; }
    1643        7453 :     xx = std::real(z);
    1644        7453 :     yy = std::imag(z);
    1645             :     //
    1646             :     //  SET PARAMETERS RELATED TO MACHINE CONSTANTS.
    1647             :     //  TOL IS THE APPROXIMATE UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 1.0E-18.
    1648             :     //  ELIM IS THE APPROXIMATE EXPONENTIAL OVER- AND UNDERFLOW LIMIT.
    1649             :     //  EXP(-ELIM).LT.EXP(-ALIM)=EXP(-ELIM)/TOL    AND
    1650             :     //  EXP(ELIM).GT.EXP(ALIM)=EXP(ELIM)*TOL       ARE INTERVALS NEAR
    1651             :     //  UNDERFLOW AND OVERFLOW LIMITS WHERE SCALED ARITHMETIC IS DONE.
    1652             :     //  RL IS THE LOWER BOUNDARY OF THE ASYMPTOTIC EXPANSION FOR LARGE Z.
    1653             :     //  DIG = NUMBER OF BASE 10 DIGITS IN TOL = 10**(-DIG).
    1654             :     //  FNUL IS THE LOWER BOUNDARY OF THE ASYMPTOTIC SERIES FOR LARGE FNU
    1655             :     //
    1656        7453 :     tol = fmax(d1mach[3], 1e-18);
    1657        7453 :     k1 = i1mach[14];
    1658        7453 :     k2 = i1mach[15];
    1659        7453 :     r1m5 = d1mach[4];
    1660        7453 :     k = ( abs(k1) > abs(k2) ? abs(k2) : abs(k1) );
    1661        7453 :     elim = 2.303 * (k*r1m5 - 3.0);
    1662        7453 :     k1 = i1mach[13] - 1;
    1663        7453 :     aa = r1m5*k1;
    1664        7453 :     dig = fmin(aa, 18.0);
    1665        7453 :     aa *= 2.303;
    1666        7453 :     alim = elim + fmax(-aa, -41.45);
    1667        7453 :     rl = 1.2 * dig + 3.0;
    1668        7453 :     fnul = 10.0 + 6.0 * (dig - 3.0);
    1669             :     //
    1670             :     // TEST FOR PROPER RANGE
    1671             :     //
    1672        7453 :     az = std::abs(z);
    1673        7453 :     fn = fnu + (n - 1);
    1674        7453 :     aa = 0.5 / tol;
    1675        7453 :     bb = i1mach[8]*0.5;
    1676        7453 :     aa = fmin(aa, bb);
    1677        7453 :     if ((az > aa) || (fn > aa)) {
    1678           1 :         *ierr = 4;
    1679           1 :         return 0;
    1680             :     }
    1681        7452 :     aa = sqrt(aa);
    1682        7452 :     if (az > aa) { *ierr = 3; }
    1683        7452 :     if (fn > aa) { *ierr = 3; }
    1684        7452 :     zn = z;
    1685        7452 :     csgn = 1.0;
    1686        7452 :     if (xx < 0.0) {
    1687        2306 :         zn = -z;
    1688             :         //
    1689             :         // CALCULATE CSGN=EXP(FNU*PI*I) TO MINIMIZE LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE
    1690             :         // WHEN FNU IS LARGE
    1691             :         //
    1692        2306 :         inu = (int)fnu;
    1693        2306 :         arg = (fnu - inu)*pi;
    1694        2306 :         if (yy < 0.0) { arg = -arg; }
    1695        2306 :         csgn = std::complex<double>(cos(arg), sin(arg));
    1696        2306 :         if (inu % 2 == 1) { csgn = -csgn; }
    1697             :     }
    1698             :     /* 40 */
    1699        7452 :     nz = binu(zn, fnu, kode, n, cy, rl, fnul, tol, elim, alim);
    1700        7452 :     if (nz < 0) {
    1701          33 :         if (nz == -2) {
    1702           0 :             *ierr = 5;
    1703           0 :             return 0;
    1704             :         }
    1705          33 :         *ierr = 2;
    1706          33 :         return 0;
    1707             :     }
    1708        7419 :     if (xx > 0.0) { return nz; }
    1709             :     //
    1710             :     // ANALYTIC CONTINUATION TO THE LEFT HALF PLANE
    1711             :     //
    1712        2297 :     nn = n - nz;
    1713        2297 :     if (nn == 0) { return nz; }
    1714             :     rtol = 1.0 / tol;
    1715             :     ascle = d1mach[0]*rtol*1e3;
    1716        4424 :     for (i = 1; i < (nn+1); i++)
    1717             :     {
    1718        2212 :         zn = cy[i-1];
    1719        2212 :         atol = 1.0;
    1720        2212 :         if (fmax(fabs(std::real(zn)), fabs(std::imag(zn))) <= ascle) {
    1721          24 :             zn *= rtol;
    1722          24 :             atol = tol;
    1723             :         }
    1724        2212 :         cy[i-1] = atol*(zn*csgn);
    1725        2212 :         csgn = -csgn;
    1726             :     }
    1727        2212 :     *ierr = 0;
    1728        2212 :     return nz;
    1729             : }
    1730             : 
    1731             : 
    1732       10532 : inline int besj(
    1733             :     std::complex<double> z,
    1734             :     double fnu,
    1735             :     int kode,
    1736             :     int n,
    1737             :     std::complex<double> *cy,
    1738             :     int *ierr
    1739             : ) {
    1740             : 
    1741             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBESJ
    1742             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    1743             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    1744             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    1745             :     //***KEYWORDS  J-BESSEL FUNCTION,BESSEL FUNCTION OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT,
    1746             :     //             BESSEL FUNCTION OF FIRST KIND
    1747             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    1748             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE THE J-BESSEL FUNCTION OF A COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    1749             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    1750             :     //
    1751             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    1752             :     //         ON KODE=1, CBESJ COMPUTES AN N MEMBER  SEQUENCE OF COMPLEX
    1753             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTIONS CY(I)=J(FNU+I-1,Z) FOR REAL, NONNEGATIVE
    1754             :     //         ORDERS FNU+I-1, I=1,...,N AND COMPLEX Z IN THE CUT PLANE
    1755             :     //         -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI. ON KODE=2, CBESJ RETURNS THE SCALED
    1756             :     //         FUNCTIONS
    1757             :     //
    1758             :     //         CY(I)=EXP(-ABS(Y))*J(FNU+I-1,Z)   I = 1,...,N , Y=AIMAG(Z)
    1759             :     //
    1760             :     //         WHICH REMOVE THE EXPONENTIAL GROWTH IN BOTH THE UPPER AND
    1761             :     //         LOWER HALF PLANES FOR Z TO INFINITY. DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION
    1762             :     //         ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS
    1763             :     //         (REF. 1).
    1764             :     //
    1765             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI,FNU ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1766             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI),  -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI
    1767             :     //           FNU    - ORDER OF INITIAL J FUNCTION, FNU.GE.0.0D0
    1768             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    1769             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    1770             :     //                             CY(I)=J(FNU+I-1,Z), I=1,...,N
    1771             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    1772             :     //                             CY(I)=J(FNU+I-1,Z)EXP(-ABS(Y)), I=1,...,N
    1773             :     //           N      - NUMBER OF MEMBERS OF THE SEQUENCE, N.GE.1
    1774             :     //
    1775             :     //         OUTPUT     CYR,CYI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    1776             :     //           CYR,CYI- DOUBLE PRECISION VECTORS WHOSE FIRST N COMPONENTS
    1777             :     //                    CONTAIN REAL AND IMAGINARY PARTS FOR THE SEQUENCE
    1778             :     //                    CY(I)=J(FNU+I-1,Z)  OR
    1779             :     //                    CY(I)=J(FNU+I-1,Z)EXP(-ABS(Y))  I=1,...,N
    1780             :     //                    DEPENDING ON KODE, Y=AIMAG(Z).
    1781             :     //           NZ     - NUMBER OF COMPONENTS SET TO ZERO DUE TO UNDERFLOW,
    1782             :     //                    NZ= 0   , NORMAL RETURN
    1783             :     //                    NZ.GT.0 , LAST NZ COMPONENTS OF CY SET  ZERO DUE
    1784             :     //                              TO UNDERFLOW, CY(I)=std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0),
    1785             :     //                              I = N-NZ+1,...,N
    1786             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    1787             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    1788             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    1789             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, AIMAG(Z)
    1790             :     //                            TOO LARGE ON KODE=1
    1791             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 LARGE - COMPUTATION DONE
    1792             :     //                            BUT LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT
    1793             :     //                            REDUCTION PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE
    1794             :     //                            ACCURACY
    1795             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 TOO LARGE - NO COMPUTA-
    1796             :     //                            TION BECAUSE OF COMPLETE LOSSES OF SIGNIFI-
    1797             :     //                            CANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    1798             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    1799             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    1800             :     //
    1801             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    1802             :     //
    1803             :     //         THE COMPUTATION IS CARRIED OUT BY THE FORMULA
    1804             :     //
    1805             :     //         J(FNU,Z)=EXP( FNU*PI*I/2)*I(FNU,-I*Z)    AIMAG(Z).GE.0.0
    1806             :     //
    1807             :     //         J(FNU,Z)=EXP(-FNU*PI*I/2)*I(FNU, I*Z)    AIMAG(Z).LT.0.0
    1808             :     //
    1809             :     //         WHERE I**2 = -1 AND I(FNU,Z) IS THE I BESSEL FUNCTION.
    1810             :     //
    1811             :     //         FOR NEGATIVE ORDERS,THE FORMULA
    1812             :     //
    1813             :     //              J(-FNU,Z) = J(FNU,Z)*COS(PI*FNU) - Y(FNU,Z)*SIN(PI*FNU)
    1814             :     //
    1815             :     //         CAN BE USED. HOWEVER,FOR LARGE ORDERS CLOSE TO INTEGERS, THE
    1816             :     //         THE FUNCTION CHANGES RADICALLY. WHEN FNU IS A LARGE POSITIVE
    1817             :     //         INTEGER,THE MAGNITUDE OF J(-FNU,Z)=J(FNU,Z)*COS(PI*FNU) IS A
    1818             :     //         LARGE NEGATIVE POWER OF TEN. BUT WHEN FNU IS NOT AN INTEGER,
    1819             :     //         Y(FNU,Z) DOMINATES IN MAGNITUDE WITH A LARGE POSITIVE POWER OF
    1820             :     //         TEN AND THE MOST THAT THE SECOND TERM CAN BE REDUCED IS BY
    1821             :     //         UNIT ROUNDOFF FROM THE COEFFICIENT. THUS, WIDE CHANGES CAN
    1822             :     //         OCCUR WITHIN UNIT ROUNDOFF OF A LARGE INTEGER FOR FNU. HERE,
    1823             :     //         LARGE MEANS FNU.GT.CABS(Z).
    1824             :     //
    1825             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    1826             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z OR FNU+N-1 IS
    1827             :     //         LARGE, LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR.
    1828             :     //         CONSEQUENTLY, IF EITHER ONE EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR), THEN
    1829             :     //         LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR FLAG
    1830             :     //         IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    1831             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    1832             :     //         IF EITHER IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS
    1833             :     //         LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT FUNCTION, ARGUMENTS
    1834             :     //         MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE LARGEST MACHINE
    1835             :     //         INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF Z AND FNU+N-1 IS
    1836             :     //         RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2, AND U3
    1837             :     //         ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE PRECISION
    1838             :     //         ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE PRECISION
    1839             :     //         ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMITING IN
    1840             :     //         THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT ONE CAN EXPECT
    1841             :     //         TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES, NO DIGITS
    1842             :     //         IN SINGLE AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC.
    1843             :     //         SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER MACHINES.
    1844             :     //
    1845             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    1846             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    1847             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    1848             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    1849             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    1850             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    1851             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    1852             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    1853             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    1854             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    1855             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    1856             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    1857             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    1858             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    1859             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    1860             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    1861             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    1862             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,

    1987             : 
    1988     2072433 : inline int besk(
    1989             :     std::complex<double> z,
    1990             :     double fnu,
    1991             :     int kode,
    1992             :     int n,
    1993             :     std::complex<double> *cy,
    1994             :     int *ierr
    1995             : ) {
    1996             : 
    1997             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBESK
    1998             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    1999             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    2000             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    2001             :     //***KEYWORDS  K-BESSEL FUNCTION,COMPLEX BESSEL FUNCTION,
    2002             :     //             MODIFIED BESSEL FUNCTION OF THE SECOND KIND,
    2003             :     //             BESSEL FUNCTION OF THE THIRD KIND
    2004             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    2005             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE K-BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2006             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    2007             :     //
    2008             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    2009             :     //
    2010             :     //         ON KODE=1, CBESK COMPUTES AN N MEMBER SEQUENCE OF COMPLEX
    2011             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTIONS CY(J)=K(FNU+J-1,Z) FOR REAL, NONNEGATIVE
    2012             :     //         ORDERS FNU+J-1, J=1,...,N AND COMPLEX Z.NE.std::complex<double>(0.0,0.0)
    2013             :     //         IN THE CUT PLANE -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI. ON KODE=2, CBESK
    2014             :     //         RETURNS THE SCALED K FUNCTIONS,
    2015             :     //
    2016             :     //         CY(J)=EXP(Z)*K(FNU+J-1,Z) , J=1,...,N,
    2017             :     //
    2018             :     //         WHICH REMOVE THE EXPONENTIAL BEHAVIOR IN BOTH THE LEFT AND
    2019             :     //         RIGHT HALF PLANES FOR Z TO INFINITY. DEFINITIONS AND
    2020             :     //         NOTATION ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL
    2021             :     //         FUNCTIONS (REF. 1).
    2022             :     //
    2023             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI,FNU ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2024             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI), Z.NE.std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0),
    2025             :     //                    -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI
    2026             :     //           FNU    - ORDER OF INITIAL K FUNCTION, FNU.GE.0.0D0
    2027             :     //           N      - NUMBER OF MEMBERS OF THE SEQUENCE, N.GE.1
    2028             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    2029             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    2030             :     //                             CY(I)=K(FNU+I-1,Z), I=1,...,N
    2031             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    2032             :     //                             CY(I)=K(FNU+I-1,Z)*EXP(Z), I=1,...,N
    2033             :     //
    2034             :     //         OUTPUT     CYR,CYI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2035             :     //           CYR,CYI- DOUBLE PRECISION VECTORS WHOSE FIRST N COMPONENTS
    2036             :     //                    CONTAIN REAL AND IMAGINARY PARTS FOR THE SEQUENCE
    2037             :     //                    CY(I)=K(FNU+I-1,Z), I=1,...,N OR
    2038             :     //                    CY(I)=K(FNU+I-1,Z)*EXP(Z), I=1,...,N
    2039             :     //                    DEPENDING ON KODE
    2040             :     //           NZ     - NUMBER OF COMPONENTS SET TO ZERO DUE TO UNDERFLOW.
    2041             :     //                    NZ= 0   , NORMAL RETURN
    2042             :     //                    NZ.GT.0 , FIRST NZ COMPONENTS OF CY SET TO ZERO DUE
    2043             :     //                              TO UNDERFLOW, CY(I)=std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0),
    2044             :     //                              I=1,...,N WHEN X.GE.0.0. WHEN X.LT.0.0
    2045             :     //                              NZ STATES ONLY THE NUMBER OF UNDERFLOWS
    2046             :     //                              IN THE SEQUENCE.
    2047             :     //
    2048             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    2049             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    2050             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    2051             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, FNU IS
    2052             :     //                            TOO LARGE OR CABS(Z) IS TOO SMALL OR BOTH
    2053             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 LARGE - COMPUTATION DONE
    2054             :     //                            BUT LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT
    2055             :     //                            REDUCTION PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE
    2056             :     //                            ACCURACY
    2057             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 TOO LARGE - NO COMPUTA-
    2058             :     //                            TION BECAUSE OF COMPLETE LOSSES OF SIGNIFI-
    2059             :     //                            CANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    2060             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    2061             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    2062             :     //
    2063             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    2064             :     //
    2065             :     //         EQUATIONS OF THE REFERENCE ARE IMPLEMENTED FOR SMALL ORDERS
    2066             :     //         DNU AND DNU+1.0 IN THE RIGHT HALF PLANE X.GE.0.0. FORWARD
    2067             :     //         RECURRENCE GENERATES HIGHER ORDERS. K IS CONTINUED TO THE LEFT
    2068             :     //         HALF PLANE BY THE RELATION
    2069             :     //
    2070             :     //         K(FNU,Z*EXP(MP)) = EXP(-MP*FNU)*K(FNU,Z)-MP*I(FNU,Z)
    2071             :     //         MP=MR*PI*I, MR=+1 OR -1, RE(Z).GT.0, I**2=-1
    2072             :     //
    2073             :     //         WHERE I(FNU,Z) IS THE I BESSEL FUNCTION.
    2074             :     //
    2075             :     //         FOR LARGE ORDERS, FNU.GT.FNUL, THE K FUNCTION IS COMPUTED
    2076             :     //         BY MEANS OF ITS UNIFORM ASYMPTOTIC EXPANSIONS.
    2077             :     //
    2078             :     //         FOR NEGATIVE ORDERS, THE FORMULA
    2079             :     //
    2080             :     //                       K(-FNU,Z) = K(FNU,Z)
    2081             :     //
    2082             :     //         CAN BE USED.
    2083             :     //
    2084             :     //         CBESK ASSUMES THAT A SIGNIFICANT DIGIT SINH(X) FUNCTION IS
    2085             :     //         AVAILABLE.
    2086             :     //
    2087             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    2088             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z OR FNU+N-1 IS
    2089             :     //         LARGE, LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR.
    2090             :     //         CONSEQUENTLY, IF EITHER ONE EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR), THEN
    2091             :     //         LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR FLAG
    2092             :     //         IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    2093             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    2094             :     //         IF EITHER IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS
    2095             :     //         LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT FUNCTION, ARGUMENTS
    2096             :     //         MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE LARGEST MACHINE
    2097             :     //         INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF Z AND FNU+N-1 IS
    2098             :     //         RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2, AND U3
    2099             :     //         ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE PRECISION
    2100             :     //         ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE PRECISION
    2101             :     //         ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMITING IN
    2102             :     //         THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT ONE CAN EXPECT
    2103             :     //         TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES, NO DIGITS
    2104             :     //         IN SINGLE AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC.
    2105             :     //         SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER MACHINES.
    2106             :     //
    2107             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    2108             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    2109             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    2110             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    2111             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    2112             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    2113             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    2114             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    2115             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    2116             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    2117             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    2118             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    2119             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    2120             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    2121             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    2122             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    2123             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    2124             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,
    2125             :     //         OR -PI/2+P.
    2126             :     //
    2127             :     //***REFERENCES  HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS BY M. ABRAMOWITZ
    2128             :     //                 AND I. A. STEGUN, NBS AMS SERIES 55, U.S. DEPT. OF
    2129             :     //                 COMMERCE, 1955.
    2130             :     //
    2131             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2132             :     //                 BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0083, MAY, 1983.
    2133             :     //
    2134             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2135             :     //                 AND LARGE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0643, MAY, 1983.
    2136             :     //
    2137             :     //               A SUBROUTINE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2138             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND85-
    2139             :     //                 1018, MAY, 1985
    2140             :     //
    2141             :     //               A PORTABLE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2142             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, TRANS.
    2143             :     //                 MATH. SOFTWARE, 1986
    2144             :     //
    2145             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  ZACON,ZBKNU,ZBUNK,ZUOIK,AZABS,I1MACH,D1MACH
    2146             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZBESK
    2147             :

    2293             : 
    2294        6920 : inline int besy(
    2295             :     std::complex<double> z,
    2296             :     double fnu,
    2297             :     int kode,
    2298             :     int n,
    2299             :     std::complex<double> *cy,
    2300             :     int *ierr
    2301             : ) {
    2302             : 
    2303             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBESY
    2304             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    2305             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    2306             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    2307             :     //***KEYWORDS  Y-BESSEL FUNCTION,BESSEL FUNCTION OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT,
    2308             :     //             BESSEL FUNCTION OF SECOND KIND
    2309             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    2310             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE THE Y-BESSEL FUNCTION OF A COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2311             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    2312             :     //
    2313             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    2314             :     //
    2315             :     //         ON KODE=1, CBESY COMPUTES AN N MEMBER SEQUENCE OF COMPLEX
    2316             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTIONS CY(I)=Y(FNU+I-1,Z) FOR REAL, NONNEGATIVE
    2317             :     //         ORDERS FNU+I-1, I=1,...,N AND COMPLEX Z IN THE CUT PLANE
    2318             :     //         -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI. ON KODE=2, CBESY RETURNS THE SCALED
    2319             :     //         FUNCTIONS
    2320             :     //
    2321             :     //         CY(I)=EXP(-ABS(Y))*Y(FNU+I-1,Z)   I = 1,...,N , Y=AIMAG(Z)
    2322             :     //
    2323             :     //         WHICH REMOVE THE EXPONENTIAL GROWTH IN BOTH THE UPPER AND
    2324             :     //         LOWER HALF PLANES FOR Z TO INFINITY. DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION
    2325             :     //         ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS
    2326             :     //         (REF. 1).
    2327             :     //
    2328             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI,FNU ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2329             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI), Z.NE.std::complex<double>(0.0D0,0.0D0),
    2330             :     //                    -PI.LT.ARG(Z).LE.PI
    2331             :     //           FNU    - ORDER OF INITIAL Y FUNCTION, FNU.GE.0.0D0
    2332             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    2333             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    2334             :     //                             CY(I)=Y(FNU+I-1,Z), I=1,...,N
    2335             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    2336             :     //                             CY(I)=Y(FNU+I-1,Z)*EXP(-ABS(Y)), I=1,...,N
    2337             :     //                             WHERE Y=AIMAG(Z)
    2338             :     //           N      - NUMBER OF MEMBERS OF THE SEQUENCE, N.GE.1
    2339             :     //           CWRKR, - DOUBLE PRECISION WORK VECTORS OF DIMENSION AT
    2340             :     //           CWRKI    AT LEAST N
    2341             :     //
    2342             :     //         OUTPUT     CYR,CYI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2343             :     //           CYR,CYI- DOUBLE PRECISION VECTORS WHOSE FIRST N COMPONENTS
    2344             :     //                    CONTAIN REAL AND IMAGINARY PARTS FOR THE SEQUENCE
    2345             :     //                    CY(I)=Y(FNU+I-1,Z)  OR
    2346             :     //                    CY(I)=Y(FNU+I-1,Z)*EXP(-ABS(Y))  I=1,...,N
    2347             :     //                    DEPENDING ON KODE.
    2348             :     //           NZ     - NZ=0 , A NORMAL RETURN
    2349             :     //                    NZ.GT.0 , NZ COMPONENTS OF CY SET TO ZERO DUE TO
    2350             :     //                    UNDERFLOW (GENERALLY ON KODE=2)
    2351             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    2352             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    2353             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    2354             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, FNU IS
    2355             :     //                            TOO LARGE OR CABS(Z) IS TOO SMALL OR BOTH
    2356             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 LARGE - COMPUTATION DONE
    2357             :     //                            BUT LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT
    2358             :     //                            REDUCTION PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE
    2359             :     //                            ACCURACY
    2360             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) OR FNU+N-1 TOO LARGE - NO COMPUTA-
    2361             :     //                            TION BECAUSE OF COMPLETE LOSSES OF SIGNIFI-
    2362             :     //                            CANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    2363             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    2364             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    2365             :     //
    2366             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    2367             :     //
    2368             :     //         THE COMPUTATION IS CARRIED OUT BY THE FORMULA
    2369             :     //
    2370             :     //         Y(FNU,Z)=0.5*(H(1,FNU,Z)-H(2,FNU,Z))/I
    2371             :     //
    2372             :     //         WHERE I**2 = -1 AND THE HANKEL BESSEL FUNCTIONS H(1,FNU,Z)
    2373             :     //         AND H(2,FNU,Z) ARE CALCULATED IN CBESH.
    2374             :     //
    2375             :     //         FOR NEGATIVE ORDERS,THE FORMULA
    2376             :     //
    2377             :     //              Y(-FNU,Z) = Y(FNU,Z)*COS(PI*FNU) + J(FNU,Z)*SIN(PI*FNU)
    2378             :     //
    2379             :     //         CAN BE USED. HOWEVER,FOR LARGE ORDERS CLOSE TO HALF ODD
    2380             :     //         INTEGERS THE FUNCTION CHANGES RADICALLY. WHEN FNU IS A LARGE
    2381             :     //         POSITIVE HALF ODD INTEGER,THE MAGNITUDE OF Y(-FNU,Z)=J(FNU,Z)*
    2382             :     //         SIN(PI*FNU) IS A LARGE NEGATIVE POWER OF TEN. BUT WHEN FNU IS
    2383             :     //         NOT A HALF ODD INTEGER, Y(FNU,Z) DOMINATES IN MAGNITUDE WITH A
    2384             :     //         LARGE POSITIVE POWER OF TEN AND THE MOST THAT THE SECOND TERM
    2385             :     //         CAN BE REDUCED IS BY UNIT ROUNDOFF FROM THE COEFFICIENT. THUS,
    2386             :     //         WIDE CHANGES CAN OCCUR WITHIN UNIT ROUNDOFF OF A LARGE HALF
    2387             :     //         ODD INTEGER. HERE, LARGE MEANS FNU.GT.CABS(Z).
    2388             :     //
    2389             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    2390             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z OR FNU+N-1 IS
    2391             :     //         LARGE, LOSSES OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR.
    2392             :     //         CONSEQUENTLY, IF EITHER ONE EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR), THEN
    2393             :     //         LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR FLAG
    2394             :     //         IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    2395             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    2396             :     //         IF EITHER IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS
    2397             :     //         LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT FUNCTION, ARGUMENTS
    2398             :     //         MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE LARGEST MACHINE
    2399             :     //         INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF Z AND FNU+N-1 IS
    2400             :     //         RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2, AND U3
    2401             :     //         ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE PRECISION
    2402             :     //         ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE PRECISION
    2403             :     //         ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMITING IN
    2404             :     //         THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT ONE CAN EXPECT
    2405             :     //         TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES, NO DIGITS
    2406             :     //         IN SINGLE AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC.
    2407             :     //         SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER MACHINES.
    2408             :     //
    2409             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    2410             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    2411             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    2412             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    2413             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    2414             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    2415             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    2416             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    2417             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    2418             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    2419             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    2420             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    2421             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    2422             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    2423             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    2424             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    2425             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    2426             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,
    2427             :     //         OR -PI/2+P.
    2428             :     //
    2429             :     //***REFERENCES  HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS BY M. ABRAMOWITZ
    2430             :     //                 AND I. A. STEGUN, NBS AMS SERIES 55, U.S. DEPT. OF
    2431             :     //                 COMMERCE, 1955.
    2432             :     //
    2433             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2434             :     //                 BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0083, MAY, 1983.
    2435             :     //
    2436             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2437             :     //                 AND LARGE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0643, MAY, 1983
    2438             :     //
    2439             :     //               A SUBROUTINE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2440             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND85-
    2441             :     //                 1018, MAY, 1985
    2442             :     //
    2443             :     //               A PORTABLE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2444             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, TRANS.
    2445             :     //                 MATH. SOFTWARE, 1986
    2446             :     //
    2447             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  ZBESH,I1MACH,D1MACH
    2448             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZBESY
    2449             : 
    2450        6920 :     std::complex<double> c1, c2, hci, st;
