    2688             : 
    2689             : 
    2690      422570 : inline std::complex<double> biry(
    2691             :     std::complex<double> z,
    2692             :     int id,
    2693             :     int kode,
    2694             :     int *ierr
    2695             : ) {
    2696             : 
    2697             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZBIRY
    2698             :     //***DATE WRITTEN   830501   (YYMMDD)
    2699             :     //***REVISION DATE  890801   (YYMMDD)
    2700             :     //***CATEGORY NO.  B5K
    2701             :     //***KEYWORDS  AIRY FUNCTION,BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF ORDER ONE THIRD
    2702             :     //***AUTHOR  AMOS, DONALD E., SANDIA NATIONAL LABORATORIES
    2703             :     //***PURPOSE  TO COMPUTE AIRY FUNCTIONS BI(Z) AND DBI(Z) FOR COMPLEX Z
    2704             :     //***DESCRIPTION
    2705             :     //
    2706             :     //                      ***A DOUBLE PRECISION ROUTINE***
    2707             :     //         ON KODE=1, CBIRY COMPUTES THE COMPLEX AIRY FUNCTION BI(Z) OR
    2708             :     //         ITS DERIVATIVE DBI(Z)/DZ ON ID=0 OR ID=1 RESPECTIVELY. ON
    2709             :     //         KODE=2, A SCALING OPTION CEXP(-AXZTA)*BI(Z) OR CEXP(-AXZTA)*
    2710             :     //         DBI(Z)/DZ IS PROVIDED TO REMOVE THE EXPONENTIAL BEHAVIOR IN
    2711             :     //         BOTH THE LEFT AND RIGHT HALF PLANES WHERE
    2712             :     //         ZTA=(2/3)*Z*CSQRT(Z)=std::complex<double>(XZTA,YZTA) AND AXZTA=ABS(XZTA).
    2713             :     //         DEFINITIONS AND NOTATION ARE FOUND IN THE NBS HANDBOOK OF
    2714             :     //         MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS (REF. 1).
    2715             :     //
    2716             :     //         INPUT      ZR,ZI ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2717             :     //           ZR,ZI  - Z=std::complex<double>(ZR,ZI)
    2718             :     //           ID     - ORDER OF DERIVATIVE, ID=0 OR ID=1
    2719             :     //           KODE   - A PARAMETER TO INDICATE THE SCALING OPTION
    2720             :     //                    KODE= 1  RETURNS
    2721             :     //                             BI=BI(Z)                 ON ID=0 OR
    2722             :     //                             BI=DBI(Z)/DZ             ON ID=1
    2723             :     //                        = 2  RETURNS
    2724             :     //                             BI=CEXP(-AXZTA)*BI(Z)     ON ID=0 OR
    2725             :     //                             BI=CEXP(-AXZTA)*DBI(Z)/DZ ON ID=1 WHERE
    2726             :     //                             ZTA=(2/3)*Z*CSQRT(Z)=std::complex<double>(XZTA,YZTA)
    2727             :     //                             AND AXZTA=ABS(XZTA)
    2728             :     //
    2729             :     //         OUTPUT     BIR,BII ARE DOUBLE PRECISION
    2730             :     //           BIR,BII- COMPLEX ANSWER DEPENDING ON THE CHOICES FOR ID AND
    2731             :     //                    KODE
    2732             :     //           IERR   - ERROR FLAG
    2733             :     //                    IERR=0, NORMAL RETURN - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    2734             :     //                    IERR=1, INPUT ERROR   - NO COMPUTATION
    2735             :     //                    IERR=2, OVERFLOW      - NO COMPUTATION, REAL(Z)
    2736             :     //                            TOO LARGE ON KODE=1
    2737             :     //                    IERR=3, CABS(Z) LARGE      - COMPUTATION COMPLETED
    2738             :     //                            LOSSES OF SIGNIFCANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION
    2739             :     //                            PRODUCE LESS THAN HALF OF MACHINE ACCURACY
    2740             :     //                    IERR=4, CABS(Z) TOO LARGE  - NO COMPUTATION
    2741             :     //                            COMPLETE LOSS OF ACCURACY BY ARGUMENT
    2742             :     //                            REDUCTION
    2743             :     //                    IERR=5, ERROR              - NO COMPUTATION,
    2744             :     //                            ALGORITHM TERMINATION CONDITION NOT MET
    2745             :     //
    2746             :     //***LONG DESCRIPTION
    2747             :     //
    2748             :     //         BI AND DBI ARE COMPUTED FOR CABS(Z).GT.1.0 FROM THE I BESSEL
    2749             :     //         FUNCTIONS BY
    2750             :     //
    2751             :     //                BI(Z)=C*SQRT(Z)*( I(-1/3,ZTA) + I(1/3,ZTA) )
    2752             :     //               DBI(Z)=C *  Z  * ( I(-2/3,ZTA) + I(2/3,ZTA) )
    2753             :     //                               C=1.0/SQRT(3.0)
    2754             :     //                             ZTA=(2/3)*Z**(3/2)
    2755             :     //
    2756             :     //         WITH THE POWER SERIES FOR CABS(Z).LE.1.0.
    2757             :     //
    2758             :     //         IN MOST COMPLEX VARIABLE COMPUTATION, ONE MUST EVALUATE ELE-
    2759             :     //         MENTARY FUNCTIONS. WHEN THE MAGNITUDE OF Z IS LARGE, LOSSES
    2760             :     //         OF SIGNIFICANCE BY ARGUMENT REDUCTION OCCUR. CONSEQUENTLY, IF
    2761             :     //         THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA=(2/3)*Z**1.5 EXCEEDS U1=SQRT(0.5/UR),
    2762             :     //         THEN LOSSES EXCEEDING HALF PRECISION ARE LIKELY AND AN ERROR
    2763             :     //         FLAG IERR=3 IS TRIGGERED WHERE UR=DMAX1(D1MACH(4),1.0D-18) IS
    2764             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION UNIT ROUNDOFF LIMITED TO 18 DIGITS PRECISION.
    2765             :     //         ALSO, IF THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA IS LARGER THAN U2=0.5/UR, THEN
    2766             :     //         ALL SIGNIFICANCE IS LOST AND IERR=4. IN ORDER TO USE THE INT
    2767             :     //         FUNCTION, ZETA MUST BE FURTHER RESTRICTED NOT TO EXCEED THE
    2768             :     //         LARGEST INTEGER, U3=I1MACH(9). THUS, THE MAGNITUDE OF ZETA
    2769             :     //         MUST BE RESTRICTED BY MIN(U2,U3). ON 32 BIT MACHINES, U1,U2,
    2770             :     //         AND U3 ARE APPROXIMATELY 2.0E+3, 4.2E+6, 2.1E+9 IN SINGLE
    2771             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC AND 1.3E+8, 1.8E+16, 2.1E+9 IN DOUBLE
    2772             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC RESPECTIVELY. THIS MAKES U2 AND U3 LIMIT-
    2773             :     //         ING IN THEIR RESPECTIVE ARITHMETICS. THIS MEANS THAT THE MAG-
    2774             :     //         NITUDE OF Z CANNOT EXCEED 3.1E+4 IN SINGLE AND 2.1E+6 IN
    2775             :     //         DOUBLE PRECISION ARITHMETIC. THIS ALSO MEANS THAT ONE CAN
    2776             :     //         EXPECT TO RETAIN, IN THE WORST CASES ON 32 BIT MACHINES,
    2777             :     //         NO DIGITS IN SINGLE PRECISION AND ONLY 7 DIGITS IN DOUBLE
    2778             :     //         PRECISION ARITHMETIC. SIMILAR CONSIDERATIONS HOLD FOR OTHER
    2779             :     //         MACHINES.
    2780             :     //
    2781             :     //         THE APPROXIMATE RELATIVE ERROR IN THE MAGNITUDE OF A COMPLEX
    2782             :     //         BESSEL FUNCTION CAN BE EXPRESSED BY P*10**S WHERE P=MAX(UNIT
    2783             :     //         ROUNDOFF,1.0E-18) IS THE NOMINAL PRECISION AND 10**S REPRE-
    2784             :     //         SENTS THE INCREASE IN ERROR DUE TO ARGUMENT REDUCTION IN THE
    2785             :     //         ELEMENTARY FUNCTIONS. HERE, S=MAX(1,ABS(LOG10(CABS(Z))),
    2786             :     //         ABS(LOG10(FNU))) APPROXIMATELY (I.E. S=MAX(1,ABS(EXPONENT OF
    2787             :     //         CABS(Z),ABS(EXPONENT OF FNU)) ). HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE MAY
    2788             :     //         HAVE ONLY ABSOLUTE ACCURACY. THIS IS MOST LIKELY TO OCCUR WHEN
    2789             :     //         ONE COMPONENT (IN ABSOLUTE VALUE) IS LARGER THAN THE OTHER BY
    2790             :     //         SEVERAL ORDERS OF MAGNITUDE. IF ONE COMPONENT IS 10**K LARGER
    2791             :     //         THAN THE OTHER, THEN ONE CAN EXPECT ONLY MAX(ABS(LOG10(P))-K,
    2792             :     //         0) SIGNIFICANT DIGITS; OR, STATED ANOTHER WAY, WHEN K EXCEEDS
    2793             :     //         THE EXPONENT OF P, NO SIGNIFICANT DIGITS REMAIN IN THE SMALLER
    2794             :     //         COMPONENT. HOWEVER, THE PHASE ANGLE RETAINS ABSOLUTE ACCURACY
    2795             :     //         BECAUSE, IN COMPLEX ARITHMETIC WITH PRECISION P, THE SMALLER
    2796             :     //         COMPONENT WILL NOT (AS A RULE) DECREASE BELOW P TIMES THE
    2797             :     //         MAGNITUDE OF THE LARGER COMPONENT. IN THESE EXTREME CASES,
    2798             :     //         THE PRINCIPAL PHASE ANGLE IS ON THE ORDER OF +P, -P, PI/2-P,
    2799             :     //         OR -PI/2+P.
    2800             :     //
    2801             :     //***REFERENCES  HANDBOOK OF MATHEMATICAL FUNCTIONS BY M. ABRAMOWITZ
    2802             :     //                 AND I. A. STEGUN, NBS AMS SERIES 55, U.S. DEPT. OF
    2803             :     //                 COMMERCE, 1955.
    2804             :     //
    2805             :     //               COMPUTATION OF BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF COMPLEX ARGUMENT
    2806             :     //                 AND LARGE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND83-0643, MAY, 1983
    2807             :     //
    2808             :     //               A SUBROUTINE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2809             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, SAND85-
    2810             :     //                 1018, MAY, 1985
    2811             :     //
    2812             :     //               A PORTABLE PACKAGE FOR BESSEL FUNCTIONS OF A COMPLEX
    2813             :     //                 ARGUMENT AND NONNEGATIVE ORDER BY D. E. AMOS, TRANS.
    2814             :     //                 MATH. SOFTWARE, 1986
    2815             :     //
    2816             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  ZBINU,AZABS,ZDIV,AZSQRT,D1MACH,I1MACH
    2817             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZBIRY

    4365             : 
    4366             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZS1S2
    4367             :     //***REFER TO  ZBESK,ZAIRY
    4368             :     //
    4369             :     //     ZS1S2 TESTS FOR A POSSIBLE UNDERFLOW RESULTING FROM THE
    4370             :     //     ADDITION OF THE I AND K FUNCTIONS IN THE ANALYTIC CON-
    4371             :     //     TINUATION FORMULA WHERE S1=K FUNCTION AND S2=I FUNCTION.
    4372             :     //     ON KODE=1 THE I AND K FUNCTIONS ARE DIFFERENT ORDERS OF
    4373             :     //     MAGNITUDE, BUT FOR KODE=2 THEY CAN BE OF THE SAME ORDER

    4375             :     //     PRECISION ABOVE THE UNDERFLOW LIMIT.

    4384      195041 :     as2 = std::abs(*s2);
    4385      195041 :     aa = std::real(*s1);
    4386      195041 :     aln = std::imag(*s1);

    4401             :         }

    4404      195041 :     if (aa > ascle) {
    4405             :         return nz;
    4406             :     }

    4415             :     std::complex<double> y,

    4419             : 
    4420             :     //***BEGIN PROLOGUE  ZUCHK

    4422             :     //
    4423             :     //      Y ENTERS AS A SCALED QUANTITY WHOSE MAGNITUDE IS GREATER THAN
    4424             :     //      EXP(-ALIM)=ASCLE=1.0E+3*D1MACH(1)/TOL. THE TEST IS MADE TO SEE
    4425             :     //      IF THE MAGNITUDE OF THE REAL OR IMAGINARY PART WOULD UNDERFLOW
    4426             :     //      WHEN Y IS SCALED (BY TOL) TO ITS PROPER VALUE. Y IS ACCEPTED
    4427             :     //      IF THE UNDERFLOW IS AT LEAST ONE PRECISION BELOW THE MAGNITUDE
    4428             :     //      OF THE LARGEST COMPONENT; OTHERWISE THE PHASE ANGLE DOES NOT HAVE
    4429             :     //      ABSOLUTE ACCURACY AND AN UNDERFLOW IS ASSUMED.
    4430             :     //
    4431             :     //***ROUTINES CALLED  (NONE)
    4432             :     //***END PROLOGUE  ZUCHK
    4433             : 
    4434          75 :     double yr = fabs(std::real(y));
    4435          75 :     double yi = fabs(std::imag(y));

    4437          75 :     double st = fmin(yr, yi);
    4438          75 :     if (st > ascle) {
    4439             :         return 0;
    4440             :     } else {
    4441          75 :         st /= tol;
    4442          75 :         if (ss < st) {
    4443             :             return 1;
    4444             :         } else {
    4445          75 :             return 0;
    4446             :         }
    4447             :     }
